        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.2c20655"><meta property="og:title" content="CuSe2 Nanocubes Enabling Efficient Sodium Storage"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.2c20655/asset/images/acsami.2c20655.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="As the most promising candidate for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), the electrochemical performance of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is highly dependent on the electrode materials. Copper selenides have established themselves as potential anode materials for SIBs due to their high theoretical capacity and good conductivity. However, the poor rate performance and fast capacity fading are the major challenges to their practical application in SIBs. Herein, single-crystalline CuSe2 nanocubes (CuSe2 NCs) are successfully synthesized via a solvothermal method. As an anode of SIBs, the CuSe2 NCs render an almost 100% initial Coulombic efficiency, an outstanding long cycle life, e.g., 380 mA h g–1 after 1700 cycles at 10 A g–1, and an unprecedented rate performance of 344 mA h g–1 at 50 A g–1. Ex situ X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns reveal the crystalline transformation of energy-storage materials, and the density functional theory (DFT) conclusion suggests that fast and stable ion diffusion kinetics enhances their electrochemical performance upon sodiation/desodiaton. The investigation into the mechanism provides a theoretical basis for subsequent practical applications."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.2c20655/asset/images/acsami.2c20655.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90da89cd5ed6b325-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da89cd5ed6b325-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: 'fcd4b568-edbe-4c68-9da6-3f353f88d8d0'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

type="text/x-mathjax-config;executed=true">MathJax.Hub.Config({
            menuSettings: {
                zoom: "Click",
                zscale: "150%"
            },
            SVG: {
                fonts: ["STIX-Web"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
            },
            "HTML-CSS": {
                fonts: ["STIX"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
                scale: 90,
            },
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("mml Jax Ready", function () {
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            MML.mi.prototype.setTeXclass = function (prev) {
                this.getPrevClass(prev);
                return this;
            };
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                setTeXclass: function (prev) {
                    this.getPrevClass(prev);
                    for (var i = 0, m = this.data.length; i < m; i++) {
                        if (this.data[i]) this.data[i].setTeXclass();
                    }
                    return this;
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("SVG Jax Ready", function () {
            var FONT = MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"] || MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"];
            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("MathML Jax Ready", function () {
            var PARSE = MathJax.InputJax.MathML.Parse;
            var ADD = PARSE.prototype.AddChildren;
            PARSE.Augment({
                AddChildren: function (mml, node) {
                    ADD.call(this, mml, node);
                    if (mml.type === 'mrow') {
                        var first = mml.data[0], last = mml.data[mml.data.length-1];
                        if (mml.open && !mml.data[0].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.open;
                        if (mml.close && !mml.data[mml.data.length - 1].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.close;
                    }
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS Jax Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax['HTML-CSS'];
            var DELIMITERS = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.DELIMITERS;
            var FONT = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"] || HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"]

            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;

            MML.mrow.Augment({
              _HTMLlineBreaks: MML.mrow.prototype.HTMLlineBreaks,
              HTMLlineBreaks: function (span) {

                if (this.parent.linebreakContainer && this.Get("display") === "inline") return false;
                return this._HTMLlineBreaks(span);
              }
            });


            DELIMITERS[0x0305] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x00AF};
            DELIMITERS[0x033F] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x003D};
            DELIMITERS[0x20E1] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x2194};

            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS multiline Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax["HTML-CSS"];
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            var PENALTY = MML.mbase.prototype.HTMLlinebreakPenalty;

            MML.msqrt.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mroot.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mspace.Augment({
                defaultDef: {
                    indentalign: MML.INDENTALIGN.AUTO,
                    indentshift: "0",
                    indenttarget: "",
                    indentalignfirst: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftfirst: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT,
                    indentalignlast: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftlast: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT
                },
                HTMLbetterBreak: function (info,state) {
                    if (info.values && info.values.id === this.spanID) {return false}
                    var values = this.getValues(
                        "linebreak",
                        "indentalign","indentshift",
                        "indentalignfirst","indentshiftfirst",
                        "indentalignlast","indentshiftlast"
                    );
                    var linebreakValue = values.linebreak;
                    if (!linebreakValue || this.hasDimAttr()) {
                        linebreakValue = MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO;
                    }
                    var W = info.scanW, span = this.HTMLspanElement(), w = span.bbox.w;
                    if (span.style.paddingLeft) {w += HTMLCSS.unEm(span.style.paddingLeft)}
                    if (W - info.shift === 0) {return false} // don't break at zero width
                    var offset = HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth - W;

                    if (state.n === 0 && (values.indentshiftfirst !== state.VALUES.indentshiftfirst ||
                        values.indentalignfirst !== state.VALUES.indentalignfirst)) {
                        var align = this.HTMLgetAlign(state,values),
                            shift = this.HTMLgetShift(state,values,align);
                        offset += (info.shift - shift);
                    }

                    var penalty = Math.floor(offset / HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth * 1000);
                    if (penalty < 0) {penalty = PENALTY.toobig - 3*penalty}
                    penalty += info.nest * PENALTY.nestfactor;

                    var linebreak = PENALTY[linebreakValue]||0;
                    if (linebreakValue === MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO && w >= PENALTY.spacelimit &&
                        !this.mathbackground && !this.background)
                    {linebreak = [(w+PENALTY.spaceoffset)*PENALTY.spacefactor]}
                    if (!MathJax.Object.isArray(linebreak)) {
                        if (linebreak || offset >= 0) {penalty = linebreak * info.nest}
                    } else {penalty = Math.max(1,penalty + linebreak[0] * info.nest)}

                    if (penalty >= info.penalty) {return false}
                    info.penalty = penalty; info.values = values; info.W = W; info.w = w;
                    values.lineleading = state.VALUES.lineleading;
                    values.linebreakstyle = "before"; values.id = this.spanID;
                    return true;
                }
            });


            
            PENALTY.goodbreak = [-400];

        <script async="" type="text/javascript" src="https://www.googletagservices.com/tag/js/gpt.js" rel="preconnect" nonce="90da89cd5ed6b325-SJC"></script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da89cd5ed6b325-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

title="Download Hi-Res Image" target="_blank" class="figure-viewer_hi-res-link"><i class="icon-file-image-o"></i><span>Download Hi-Res Image</span></a><span class="fv-separator"></span><a href="#" title="Download to MS-PowerPoint" class="figure-viewer_ms-p-link"><i class="icon-file-powerpoint-o"></i><span>Download to MS-PowerPoint</span></a><span class="cit-this-container"><a href="/action/showCitFormats?doi=10.1021/acsami.2c20655&amp;href=/doi/10.1021/acsami.2c20655" title="Cite This" class="figure-viewer-cite-this-link"><i class="icon-check-circle"></i><span><strong>Cite Interfaces</i></span><span class="cit-fg-year"> 2023</span><span class="cit-fg-volume">, 15</span><span class="cit-fg-issue">, 10</span><span class="cit-fg-pageRange">, 12976-12985</span></span></span></div></div></div></div></div><input type="hidden" name="aamick" id="copyRights" value="/pb-assets/json/journal-info-1738791784303.json"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone5" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone5"><!-- Article Refresh Event Tracking -->
<script nonce="90da89cd5ed6b325-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "CuSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Enabling Efficient Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c20655", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "CuSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Enabling Efficient Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c20655", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "CuSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Enabling Efficient Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c20655", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "CuSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Enabling Efficient Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c20655", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "CuSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Enabling Efficient Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c20655", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "CuSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Enabling Efficient Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c20655", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "CuSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Enabling Efficient Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c20655", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "CuSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Enabling Efficient Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c20655", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "CuSe&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; Nanocubes Enabling Efficient Sodium Storage", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.2c20655", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

data-id="article_author_search">Chenxi Liu</a></span></div></div></div></span></li><li><span><span class="hlFld-ContribAuthor" tabindex="0" data-id="article_author_info" property="author">Yurong Yan</span><div class="loa-info hlFld-Affiliation"><div class="loa-info--wrapper"><div class="loa-info-name">Yurong Yan</div><div class="loa-info-affiliations"><div class="loa-info-affiliations-info">School of Materials Science and Engineering, South China University of Technology, Guangzhou 510641, China</div></div><div class="loa-info-scifinder"><span>More by <a href="/action/doSearch?field1=Contrib&amp;text1=Yurong++Yan" data-id="article_author_search">Yurong Yan</a></span></div><div class="loa-info-orcid"><img height="20" width="27" Wu</span><strong>*</strong><div class="loa-info hlFld-Affiliation"><div class="loa-info--wrapper"><div class="loa-info-name">Songping Wu</div><div class="loa-info-affiliations"><div class="loa-info-affiliations-info">School of Chemistry and Chemical Engineering, South China University of Technology, Guangzhou 510641, China</div><div class="loa-info-affiliations-info">Guangdong Key Laboratory of Fuel Cell Technology, Guangzhou 510641, China</div></div><span class="conrtib-corresp"></span><span class="conrtib-corresp"></span><span class="conrtib-corresp"><strong>*</strong>Email: <a href="mailto:chwsp@scut.edu.cn">chwsp@scut.edu.cn</a></span><div class="loa-info-scifinder"><span>More by <a href="/action/doSearch?field1=Contrib&amp;text1=Songping++Wu" data-id="article_author_search">Songping Wu</a></span></div><div class="loa-info-orcid"><img height="20" width="27" issue&nbsp;</span><time datetime="2023-03-15" class="article__history__time">15 March 2023</time></li></ul></div></div></div></div></div><div class="hidden" property="articleSection">research-article</div><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2023 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_rightPermissionsLink"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone4" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone4"><div class="articleRightsPermissionsLink"><a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D12976%26pageCount%3D10%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DQi%2BZhu%252C%2BAnding%2BXu%252C%2BHuaming%2BChen%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D15%26issueNum%3D10%26contentID%3Dacsami.2c20655%26title%3DCuSe2%2BNanocubes%2BEnabling%2BEfficient%2BSodium%2BStorage%26numPages%3D10%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D12985%26publicationDate%3DMarch%2B2023" data-id="article_rights_permissions">Request reuse permissions</a></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_header-metrics-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="article_header-metrics-dropzone"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.2c20655/asset/images/medium/am2c20655_0008.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.2c20655/asset/images/large/am2c20655_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.2c20655&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">As the most promising candidate for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), the electrochemical performance of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is highly dependent on the electrode materials. Copper selenides have established themselves as potential anode materials for SIBs due to their high theoretical capacity and good conductivity. However, the poor rate performance and fast capacity fading are the major challenges to their practical application in SIBs. Herein, single-crystalline CuSe<sub>2</sub> nanocubes (CuSe<sub>2</sub> NCs) are successfully synthesized via a solvothermal method. As an anode of SIBs, the CuSe<sub>2</sub> NCs render an almost 100% initial Coulombic efficiency, an outstanding long cycle life, e.g., 380 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> after 1700 cycles at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>, and an unprecedented rate performance of 344 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 50 A g<sup>–1</sup>. Ex situ X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns reveal the crystalline transformation of energy-storage materials, and the density functional theory (DFT) conclusion suggests that fast and stable ion diffusion kinetics enhances their electrochemical performance upon sodiation/desodiaton. The investigation into the mechanism provides a theoretical basis for subsequent practical applications.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D12976%26pageCount%3D10%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DQi%2BZhu%252C%2BAnding%2BXu%252C%2BHuaming%2BChen%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D15%26issueNum%3D10%26contentID%3Dacsami.2c20655%26title%3DCuSe2%2BNanocubes%2BEnabling%2BEfficient%2BSodium%2BStorage%26numPages%3D10%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D12985%26publicationDate%3DMarch%2B2023" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2023 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20batteries">sodium-ion batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Anode+Materials&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_anode%20materials">anode materials</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Cuse2+Nanocubes&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_CuSe2%20nanocubes">CuSe<sub>2</sub> nanocubes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Rate+Performance&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_rate%20performance">rate performance</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Reaction+Mechanism&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_reaction%20mechanism">reaction mechanism</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">1.  Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">As an efficient energy-storage device, lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have been extensively investigated and widely applied in electric vehicles, portable electronic devices, and smart grids due to their high energy density, stable long-life cyclability, and environmental benignity. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2" aria-label="reference 1 and 2">(1,2)</a> However, the insufficient and uneven distribution of lithium resources on earth (0.0017 wt %) and ever-increasing cost have restricted their utilization in next-generation large-scale energy-storage systems. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3" aria-label="reference 3">(3)</a> In the past decades, many efforts have been devoted to exploring alternatives to LIBs using earth-abundant and cheap materials. Among all of the candidates, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have received increasing attention owing to their similar operating mechanism, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4" aria-label="reference 4">(4)</a> abundant reserves, and cheap price. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5" aria-label="reference 5">(5)</a> Unfortunately, the larger ion radius of Na<sup>+</sup> and heavier molar mass inevitably caused sluggish reaction kinetics and huge volume expansion as compared with Li<sup>+</sup>, which led to poor rate performance, short cycling life, and low output capacity of SIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6" aria-label="reference 6">(6)</a> Note that the low initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) of hosts of sodium is another ubiquitously formidable and easily overlooked problem. Low ICE is bound to add injury to the inherent shortcomings of sodium-ion batteries, i.e., low energy density. Therefore, it becomes of urgent importance to explore appropriate electrode materials possessing high ICE, stable reversible ion insertion/extraction, and high-rate performance.</div><div class="NLM_p">As we know, the performance of SIBs is in close relation to electrode materials. Among the tremendous reported materials, transition metal selenides (TMSes), such as MoSe<sub>2</sub>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7 ref8'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7 ref8" aria-label="reference 7 and 8">(7,8)</a> CoSe<sub>2</sub>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9" aria-label="reference 9">(9)</a> ZnSe, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10 ref11'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10 ref11" aria-label="reference 10 and 11">(10,11)</a> FeSe<sub>2</sub>, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12 ref13 ref14'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12 ref13 ref14" aria-label="reference 12 to 14">(12−14)</a> and Cu<sub>2</sub>Se <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15 ref16 ref17'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15 ref16 ref17" aria-label="reference 15 to 17">(15−17)</a> have attracted considerable attention as promising anode materials of SIBs owing to their high theoretical capacity and excellent redox reversibility. Particularly, copper selenides have appealed great interest due to their high electrochemical activity and superior electrical conductivity. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18 ref19'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref19" aria-label="reference 18 and 19">(18,19)</a> Compared with hard carbon, as a member of insertion-type electrodes, which is largely limited by the low theoretical capacity, CuSe<sub>2</sub> has attracted wide attention because of its high reversible capacity. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a> CuSe<sub>2</sub>, as a transition metal selenide, exhibits better reversibility and superior electronic conductivities than oxides/sulfides because of the weaker electronegative and the larger ionic radius of Se. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23" aria-label="reference 20 to 23">(20−23)</a> In addition, compared to alloying-type materials, such as P, Sn, and Sb, CuSe<sub>2</sub> has higher initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24 ref25 ref26 ref27'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24 ref25 ref26 ref27" aria-label="reference 24 to 27">(24−27)</a> Nevertheless, some critical issues, concentrating on sluggish ion transportation, huge volume expansion, and drastic structural reorganizations, have been hindering the further development of copper selenides for their efficient service as the anode of SIBs.</div><div class="NLM_p">Recently, some strategies have been made to improve the comprehensive applicability of selenium-based electrodes, such as nanocrystallization, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref29'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref29" aria-label="reference 28 and 29">(28,29)</a> morphology regulation, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9 ref30'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9 ref30" aria-label="reference 9 and 30">(9,30)</a> and hybrid composite construction. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31 ref32'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31 ref32" aria-label="reference 31 and 32">(31,32)</a> For example, Yue et al. synthesized Cu<sub>2</sub>Se@PPy via in situ coating conductive polymer carbon, which delivered a high specific capacity (293.0 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 1.0 A g<sup>–1</sup>) and rate performance (263.5 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16" aria-label="reference 16">(16)</a> Similar performance has been confirmed in another reference. Li et al. designed the mesoporous Cu<sub>2–<i>x</i></sub>Se nanocrystals, acting as a SIB anode, and presented a capacity retention of 88% after 3000 cycles at 5 A g<sup>–1</sup> (212.4 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>) and 92.1% at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup> in the rate test (∼230.5 mA h g<sup>–1</sup>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18" aria-label="reference 18">(18)</a> High current density was also utilized to check the capability of fighting against current shock for the Cu–Se system. Xiao et al. fabricated Cu<sub>2</sub>Se-CTAB nanosheet arrays with expanded interlayer space, revealing high discharge capacity and rate performance, e.g., 426.0 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> and 238.1 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 30 A g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17" aria-label="reference 17">(17)</a> Although some progress has been made, sodium-ion anode materials, with high initial Coulombic efficiency and the endurance of withstanding the long-time impact of extremely high current density, are still very rare to date. Accordingly, exploiting new materials has become urgent for tackling the coming application requirements.</div><div class="NLM_p last">Here, we have successfully synthesized a single-crystalline CuSe<sub>2</sub> nanocube material (CuSe<sub>2</sub> NCs) via a polyol solution chemical method using easily available reagents. The neat arrangement of atoms in single-crystalline CuSe<sub>2</sub> could facilitate sodium-ion transport and reduce the energy barrier for ion diffusion. The obtained CuSe<sub>2</sub> showed a nanoscale cube morphology, which is conducive to the penetration of the electrolyte and alleviates the volume expansion in the process of cycling. Combining these merits, the CuSe<sub>2</sub> NCs exhibit an almost 100% ICE, an outstanding long cycle life (380 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> after 1700 cycles at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup>), and unprecedented rate performance (344 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> at 50 A g<sup>–1</sup>) when applied in SIBs. So far, there is no report about Cu–Se as an anode of SIBs that could achieve such excellent rate performance when cycled at an extremely high current density of 50 A g<sup>–1</sup>. More importantly, we have revealed the reaction mechanism via ex situ X-ray diffraction (XRD) patterns combined with the theoretical calculation, which provided a good reference for subsequent researchers.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">2.  Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.1.  Synthesis of CuSe<sub>2</sub> Nanocubes (CuSe<sub>2</sub> NCs)</h3><div class="NLM_p">All reagents were of analytical grade and used without further purification, and were all commercially available. CuSe<sub>2</sub> nanocubes were prepared as previously reported with some modifications. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33" aria-label="reference 33">(33)</a> In the typical synthesis process, 0.1279 g of CuCl<sub>2</sub>·2H<sub>2</sub>O was added into 30 mL of triethylene glycol (TEG) and stirred vigorously for 1 h in a beaker to obtain a homogeneous copper precursor solution. Subsequently, 0.1184 g of Se powder and 0.1 g of poly(vinylpyrrolidone) (PVP) were added to 120 mL of TEG under vigorous stirring in a three-neck flask, which was attached to a reflux condenser. The mixture was purged with Ar for 20 min and then heated to 210 °C with an electric jacket. Then, the copper precursor solution and 15 μL of triethylenetetramine (TETA) were quickly injected into the Se precursor solution in turn, which was continuously stirred for 45 min at 210 °C. During the whole reaction process, it was necessary to keep a flow of Ar through the three-neck flask to drive oxygen out. After the reaction, the solution was cooled to room temperature by water-bath quenching. After centrifugation followed by washing using ethanol three times (8000 rpm, 2 min) to remove any possible impurities, the sample was finally dried at 60 °C for 12 h in a vacuum to obtain the CuSe<sub>2</sub> nanocubes. Bulk orthorhombic CuSe<sub>2</sub> particles have been synthesized using a Cu<sub>2</sub>O template for comparison (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.2c20655/suppl_file/am2c20655_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>).</div><div id="sec2_1_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_3"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h4 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.1.1.  Material Characterization</h4><div class="NLM_p last">The X-ray diffraction (XRD) analyses of the as-obtained samples were recorded on an advanced X-ray diffractometer (D8 Advance, Bruker, Germany) with Cu Kα radiation. Raman scattering spectra were recorded with a Raman spectrometer (LabRAM Aramis, HJY, France). The sample composite and elements valence were characterized by an X-ray photoelectron spectrometer (XPS, Kratos Axis Ultra DLD, Japan) with a standard Al Kα source (1486.6 eV). The morphology and particle sizes of the as-synthesized samples were detected by a scanning electron microscope (SEM, Zeiss Ultra 55) and a transmission electron microscope (TEM, JEM-2100HR, Tokyo, Japan).</div></div><div id="sec2_1_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_3"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h4 class="article-section__title" id="_i6">2.1.2.  Electrochemical Measurements</h4><div class="NLM_p last">The CuSe<sub>2</sub> NC electrode was prepared by a slurry-coating method. Typically, as-prepared samples, carbon black (Super P), and sodium carboxymethyl cellulose (CMC) were ground at a mass ratio of 8:1:1 in deionized water to form a homogeneous slurry, which was subsequently coated on a Cu foil with a mass loading of 0.6–0.8 mg cm<sup>–2</sup>. The coin cells (CR2016) were assembled in an Ar-filled glovebox (Etelux, Lab2000, Beijing, China) with sodium metal as a counter electrode, glass fiber as a separator, and 1 M NaCF<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>3</sub> in diethylene glycol dimethyl ether (DGM) as an electrolyte. The galvanostatic charging/discharging measurements were performed at a voltage range of 0.3–3 V at 25 °C. Cyclic voltammetry (CV) measurements were conducted on an electrochemical workstation (CHI600E, Shanghai, China) with a scan rate of 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup> in the range of 0.3–3 V. Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) was performed on the same electrochemical workstation with a frequency range of 0.01 Hz–100 kHz. The galvanostatic intermittent titrations (GITT) were acquired after 50 cycles at 10 A g<sup>–1</sup> with a pulse current of 500 mA g<sup>–1</sup> for 4 min and rest intervals of 30 min.</div></div><div id="sec2_1_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_3"><div id="ac_i7" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h4 class="article-section__title" id="_i7">2.1.3.  Computational Method</h4><div class="NLM_p last">Density functional theory (DFT) calculations were conducted using the Vienna Ab initio Simulation Package. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34 ref35'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34 ref35" aria-label="reference 34 and 35">(34,35)</a> The Perdew–Burke–Ernzerhof (PBE) form of generalized gradient approximation (GGA) was chosen as the exchange–correlation potential. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36" aria-label="reference 36">(36)</a> The Brillouin zone was sampled using the 5 × 5 × 5 and 9 × 7 × 5 Monkhorst–Pack <i>k</i>-point meshes and 500 eV cutoff energy for the cubic and orthorhombic crystal structure optimization, respectively. All of the atoms were permitted to relax as supported by the conjugated gradient method, where the convergence threshold and maximum force were set to be 10<sup>–5</sup> eV for energy and 0.02 eV Å<sup>–1</sup> for ionic relaxation, respectively. Electrochemical properties and the lattice structure of Na in the CuSe<sub>2</sub> supercell (2 × 2 × 2 for cubic and 3 × 2 × 2 for orthorhombic) have also been explored. Because of the heavily correlated Cu atom in the CuSe<sub>2</sub>, this part used DFT + <i>U</i> methodology in which <i>U</i> was selected for the localized 3d electrons of Cu, and the <i>U</i><sub>eff</sub> was set to 4 eV according to previous research. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37 ref38'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37 ref38" aria-label="reference 37 and 38">(37,38)</a> The formation energy (Δ<i>E</i>) of Na occupying the interstitial position was calculated as<div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq1"><div MJX_Assistive_MathML_Block" role="presentation"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mi
