                        cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polyrrole-encapsulated Cu2Se nanosheets in situ grown on Cu mesh for high stability sodium-ion battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yue, Luchao; Wang, Dong; Wu, Zhenguo; Zhao, Wenxi; Ren, Yuchun; Zhang, Longcheng; Zhong, Benhe; Li, Na; Tang, Bo; Liu, Qian; Luo, Yonglan; Asiri, Abdullah M.; Guo, Xiaodong; Sun, Xuping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">433</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">Part_1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">134477</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Copper selenide (Cu2Se) features high theor. capacity and quasi-2D characteristics built by repeating sextuple layers of Se-Cu-Cu-Cu-Cu-Se, making it a fascinating anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, it experiences huge vol. variation during repeated discharge-charge processes.  Here, a productive approach to preserve the structure of Cu2Se anode via in-situ coating conductive polymer carbon is proposed.  As a demonstration, Cu2Se nanosheets encapsulated by polypyrrole (PPy) were anchored on Cu mesh (Cu2Se@PPy) and regarded as an electrode material for SIBs.  The PPy shell enjoys double functions that improves the electronic cond. as well as alleviates the significant vol. swelling of Cu2Se.  As a result, Cu2Se@PPy gives a satisfactory electrochem. performance, including high specific capacity of 293.0 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1, impressive rate capacity (263.5 mAh g-1 under 10.0 A g-1 over 2000 cycles).  This work describes the uncomplicated approaches available for designing high stability metal selenides anodes for sodium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoBR12KUUlP5LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0livO5uPbDmYkg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Nanosheet Array of Cu2Se Intercalation Compound with Expanded Interlayer Space for Sodium Ion Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Yuanhua; Zhao, Xiaobing; Wang, Xuezhao; Su, Dangcheng; Bai, Shuo; Chen, Wei; Fang, Shaoming; Zhou, Liming; Cheng, Hui-Ming; Li, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">25</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2000666</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Intercalation chem./engineering has been widely investigated in the development of electrochem. energy storage.  Graphite, as an old intercalation host, is receiving vigorous attention again via a new halogen intercalation.  Whereas, exploiting new intercalation hosts and optimizing the intercalation effect still remains a great challenge.  This study fabricates a Cu2Se intercalation compd. showing expanded interlayer space and nanosheet array features by using a green growth approach, in which cetyltrimethyl ammonium bromide (CTAB) is inserted into Cu2Se at an ambient temp.  When acting as an electrode material for sodium-ion batteries, the Cu2Se-CTAB nanosheet arrays exhibit excellent discharge capacity and rate capability (426.0 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and 238.1 mAh g-1 at 30 A g-1), as well as high capacity retention of ~ 90% at 20 A g-1 after 6500 cycles.  Benefiting from the porous array architecture, the transport of electrolytes is facilitated on the surface of Cu2Se nanosheets.  In particular, the CTAB intercalated in the interlayer space of Cu2Se can increase its buffer space, stabilize the polyselenide shuttle, and prevent the fast growth of Cu nanoparticles during its electrochem. process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIkG1ZmQxQOLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0livO5uPbDmYkg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal selenides for high performance sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Minghe; Yu, Haoxiang; Hu, Feiyang; Liu, Tingting; Cheng, Xing; Zheng, Runtian; Bai, Ying; Shui, Miao; Shu, Jie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">380</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">122557</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review is given.  In consideration of the abundance of Na resources, Na ion batteries (SIBs) have been revisited recently and are considered as a substitution for Li ion batteries (LIBs).  Among all the proposed anodes for SIBs, metal selenides labeled as high theor. capacity materials have aroused the interest of battery researchers.  However, as conversion/alloying based electrode materials, metal selenides suffer from a severe vol. change during cycling, thus leading to kinetic problems and poor electrochem. stability, which restrain their further application in SIBs.  Therefore, modification strategies such as coupling with carbonaceous material, designing unique structure, selecting an upper cut-off voltage, optimizing the compn. of electrolyte, controlling the compn. of the material etc. have been adopted to alleviate the vol. change issue of metal selenides electrodes.  The research progresses on the metal selenides as electrodes for SIBs are outlined and the difference and necessity of each metal selenide from the perspectives of structure and cond. are emphasized.  The summarization of metal selenides contains the synthesis methods, modification methods for performance improvement, corresponding reaction mechanism and performance in full-cell system.  A conclusion with the challenges and outlook of metal selenides in the field of SIBs is also presented.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoNNZ4p-AFnU7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0livO5uPbDmYkg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhs12gtrzN&amp;md5=c06a8ec21d642cabc24de35626fef627</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2019.104389"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.-F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pam, M.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Constructing stress-release layer on Fe7Se8-based composite for highly stable sodium-storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Song; Huang, Shaozhuan; Zhang, Yuan-Fang; Fan, Shuang; Yan, Dong; Shang, Yang; Pam, Mei Er; Ge, Qi; Shi, Yumeng; Yang, Hui Ying</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">69</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Engineering multicomponent composite materials into tailored structure is of vital importance for developing advanced sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  However, the mech. stress intensification originating from severe vol. expansion upon sodiation induces anisotropic swelling and anomalous structural changes, thus leading to electrode instability and inferior sodium storage performance.  Herein, we propose a novel stress-release strategy by inserting of MoSe2 nanosheets onto the surface of yolk-shell Fe7Se8@C composite to accommodate the vol. expansion and stabilize the electrode.  Bestowed by the unique superiority, the Fe7Se8@C@MoSe2 composite manifests impressive sodium-storage performance in terms of high specific capacity (473.3 mAh g-1 at 0.1 A g-1), excellent rate capability (274.5 mAh g-1 at 5.0 A g-1) and long-term cycling stability (87.1% capacity retention after 600 cycles at 1.0 A g-1).  Finite element (FE) simulations confirm that the exterior MoSe2 layer could significantly dissipate the stress caused by the sodiation-induced expansion of Fe7Se8 in the carbon layer.  The primary sodium storage mechanisms and structural evolution are further revealed in details by in situ and ex situ investigations.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr_RwYObRRWALVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgOjcTKcpyw0A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXisVyhsbrL&amp;md5=6175a87b236e578e8e8a0c5d0ead4996</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201801765"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tailoring Rod-Like FeSe<sub>2</sub> Coated with Nitrogen-Doped Carbon for High-Performance Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Adv. The results demonstrated that the Sn4+xP3·(Sn-P) electrode using CMC binder delivered an initial discharge capacity of 1030 mA h g-1 and a reversible charge capacity of 892 mA h g-1, at the c.d. of 100 mA g-1.  The addn. of 5% FEC to the electrolyte can improve the cycling stability of the Sn4+xP3 electrode exhibited superior high rate capability, with a stable capacity of 165 mA h g-1 at the 10 C rate (5000 mA g-1).  All the resultes indicate that Sn4+xP3·(Sn-P) would be a promising anode material candidate for sodium-ion batteries with low cost, long cycling stability, and relatively good rate capability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqoO0b7cRbjN7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgOjcTKcpyw0A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXmtVCltrc%253D&amp;md5=23a94da04c3e013a5ccccde96ec89b03</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201402943"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrasmall Sn Nanoparticles Embedded in Carbon as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrasmall Sn Nanoparticles Embedded in Carbon as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yongchang; Zhang, Ning; Jiao, Lifang; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">214-220</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Designed as a high-capacity, high-rate, and long-cycle life anode for Na-ion batteries, ultra-small Sn nanoparticles (≈8 nm) homogeneously embedded in spherical C network (denoted as 8-Sn@C) is prepd. using an aerosol spray pyrolysis method.  Instrumental analyses show that 8-Sn@C nanocomposite with 46% Sn and a BET surface area of 150.43 m2 g-1 delivers an initial reversible capacity of ≈493.6 mA h g-1 at the c.d. of 200 mA g-1, a high-rate capacity of 349 mA h g-1 even at 4000 mA g-1, and a stable capacity of ≈415 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles at 1000 mA g-1.  The remarkable electrochem. performance of 8-Sn@C is owing to the synergetic effects between the well-dispersed ultra-small Sn nanoparticles and the conductive C network.  This unique structure of very-fine Sn nanoparticles embedded in the porous C network can effectively suppress the vol. fluctuation and particle aggregation of Sn during prolonged sodiation/desodiation process, thus solving the major problems of pulverization, loss of elec. contact and low use rate facing Sn anode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIJZ-8q45agLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgOjcTKcpyw0A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXltVKksA%253D%253D&amp;md5=bf146b366c93613b170938edd33ec0fe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1021/ja310347x"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Darwiche, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Marino, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sougrati, M.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Better Cycling Performances of Bulk Sb in Na-Ion Batteries Compared to Li-Ion Systems: An Unexpected Electrochemical Mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Darwiche, Ali; Marino, Cyril; Sougrati, Moulay T.; Fraisse, Bernard; Stievano, Lorenzo; Monconduit, Laure</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">134</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">51</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20805-20811</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pure micrometric antimony can be successfully used as neg. electrode material in Na-ion batteries, sustaining a capacity close to 600 mAh g-1 at a high rate with a Coulombic efficiency of 99 over 160 cycles, an extremely high capacity compared to any other compd. tested against both Li and Na.  The reaction mechanism with Na does not simply go through the alloying mechanism obsd. for Li where the intermediate species are those expected from the phase diagram.  In the case of Na, the intermediate phases are mostly amorphous and could not be precisely identified.  Surprisingly, it is evidenced that a competition takes place at the end of the discharge of the Sb/Na cell between the formation of the hexagonal and the cubic polymorphs of Na3Sb, the last being described in the literature as unstable at atm. pressure and only synthesized under high pressure (1-9 GPa).  In addn., fluoroethylene carbonate added to the electrolyte combined with an appropriate electrode formulation based on CM-cellulose, carbon black, and vapor ground carbon fibers seems to be determinant in the excellent performances of this material.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpfZ6rvnJyfxrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liILac_Vno8PA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amorphous, Crystalline and Crystalline/Amorphous Selenium Nanowires and Their Different (De)Lithiation Mechanisms</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Xiaoming; Gao, Peng; Sun, Shuchao; Bao, Di; Wang, Ying; Li, Xiaobo; Wu, Tingting; Chen, Yujin; Yang, Piaoping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6730-6736</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Selenium is applied as the cathode material of lithium/selenium (Li-Se) battery, which has high theor. volumetric capacity d. (3253 mA h/cm3) and high output voltages.  However, it has a low m.p. (494 K) and a large sensitivity to thermal treatment, which often result in the phase transition between cryst. Se (trigonal phase) and amorphous Se during the charge/discharge cycles of Li-Se battery as reported in literatures.  In order to clarify the different chem. (de)lithiation mechanisms between them in Li-Se battery, in this work large-area amorphous selenium (a-Se) nanowires (NWs) have been successfully prepd. first through a facile high-energy ball-milling method.  Subsequently the cryst. (c) and cryst./amorphous (c/a) selenium NWs have also been prepd. through annealing the above as-obtained amorphous products, resp.  The affirmative compn. and morphol. of the as-obtained Se nanostructures have been demonstrated by the XRD, SEM, TEM, HRTEM and Raman spectra measurements.  And their sp. surface area and pore size distribution have also been analyzed by BET measurements.  Finally, it is proved that the as-obtained NWs used as the cathode material of Li-Se battery displayed different chem. reaction processes with Li+ and the related various storage capacities (a-Se: 755 mAh/g, c/a-Se: 705 mAh/g, c-Se: 250 mAh/g).  This work has helped us to better understand and correlate the formation of intermediate phases with the electrochem. performance of Li-Se cells and shines new light on how to improve the cell performance by turning the phase of Se.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqWGXsUCVRJbbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liILac_Vno8PA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsFejt7bM&amp;md5=06e2ca8f56d55ee38c6a3357574cab4a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1007/s11581-017-2164-0"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Facile fabrication of selenium (Se) nanowires for enhanced lithium storage in Li-Se battery</span>. <i>Ionics</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>23</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3571</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3579</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A cost-effective facile approach has been developed to prep.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hybrid hierarchical micro/nanostructures possess great potential in engineering of advanced electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, a sandwich hierarchical architecture composed of ZnSe nanoparticles fastened in N-doped carbon polyhedra anchoring onto graphene with the modification of MoSe2 nanosheets (ZnSe⊂N-C@MoSe2/rGO) is synthesized by a self-template and subsequent selenization strategy.  Due to the distinctive architectural and multicompositional features, these hybrids deliver a high reversible capacity of 319.4 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 for 1800 cycles, 206.5 mA h g-1 at 6 A g-1 for 2800 cycles, and 177.7 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1 for 5000 cycles, as well as a better rate capability up to 10 A g-1 with a reversible capacity of 224.4 mAh g-1 as an anode material for SIBs.  By comparing the capacity contribution, electrochem. impedance spectra and DNa+ of different materials, the advantages of ZnSe⊂N-C@MoSe2/rGO are confirmed.  The sodium storage mechanism of hybrids is further revealed by in situ X-ray diffraction patterns and high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy results.  The improved sodium storage properties of hybrids manifest the significance of elaborate construction of novel multicomponent hierarchical architectures with higher complexity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo3KMObSzX9arVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liILac_Vno8PA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvVGgsLzL&amp;md5=dddc9adb82cc51a2dc6b5c1763ce1e9e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA09676C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, S.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, J.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The rational design of cathode materials for lithium-selenium (Li-Se) batteries is essential to achieve high-performance electrochem. properties with long cycle life and excellent rate capability.  In this paper, novel porous carbon nanofibers with bimodal pores (micro/meso), as efficient cathode hosts for Li-Se batteries, were successfully synthesized by carbonization of electrospun zeolitic imidazole framework-8/polyacrylonitrile (ZIF-8/PAN) nanofibers and further chem. activation.  Mesopores originated from carbonization of ZIF-8 embedded in the carbon nanofiber, and micropores were further introduced via KOH activation.  During the activation step, micropores were introduced to the ZIF-8-derived meso porous carbon cages and within the carbon nanofibers, resulting in the formation of bimodal porous carbon nanofibers with enlarged pore vols.  Owing to their mesopores for easy access of electrolyte and high utilization of chain-like selenium with low-range ordering within the micropore, the selenium-loaded bimodal porous carbon nanofibers exhibited high discharge capacity and superb rate performance.  The discharge capacities of the nanofibers at the 2nd and 300th cycle at a c.d. of 0.5C were 742 and 588 mA h g-1, resp.  The capacity retention calcd. from the 2nd cycle was 79.2%.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Efficiency of ab-initio total energy calculations for metals and semiconductors using a plane-wave basis set</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kresse, G.; Furthmuller, J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Computational Materials Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1996</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors present a detailed description and comparison of algorithms for performing ab-initio quantum-mech. calcns. using pseudopotentials and a plane-wave basis set.  The authors will discuss: (a) partial occupancies within the framework of the linear tetrahedron method and the finite temp. d.-functional theory, (b) iterative methods for the diagonalization of the Kohn-Sham Hamiltonian and a discussion of an efficient iterative method based on the ideas of Pulay's residual minimization, which is close to an order N2atoms scaling even for relatively large systems, (c) efficient Broyden-like and Pulay-like mixing methods for the charge d. including a new special preconditioning optimized for a plane-wave basis set, (d) conjugate gradient methods for minimizing the electronic free energy with respect to all degrees of freedom simultaneously.  The authors have implemented these algorithms within a powerful package called VAMP (Vienna ab-initio mol.-dynamics package).  The program and the techniques have been used successfully for a large no. of different systems (liq. and amorphous semiconductors, liq. simple and transition metals, metallic and semi-conducting surfaces, phonons in simple metals, transition metals and semiconductors) and turned out to be very reliable.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqLsfJmf_ZpQLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg2z__9-3TzQA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK28XmtFWgsrk%253D&amp;md5=779b9a71bbd32904f968e39f39946190</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.54.11169"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kresse, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Furthmüller, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Efficient iterative schemes for ab initio total-energy calculations using a plane-wave basis set</span>. <i>Phys.                 10.1103/PhysRevB.54.11169</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D54%26publication_year%3D1996%26pages%3D11169-11186%26journal%3DPhys.%2BRev.%2BB%26author%3DG.%2BKresse%26author%3DJ.%2BFurthm%25C3%25BCller%26title%3DEfficient%2Biterative%2Bschemes%2Bfor%2Bab%2Binitio%2Btotal-energy%2Bcalculations%2Busing%2Ba%2Bplane-wave%2Bbasis%2Bset%26doi%3D10.1103%252FPhysRevB.54.11169&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.2c20655&amp;doiOfLink=10.1103%2FPhysRevB.54.11169&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Efficient iterative schemes for ab initio total-energy calculations using a plane-wave basis set</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kresse, G.; Furthmueller, J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review B: Condensed Matter</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1996</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">54</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">16</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11169-11186</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PRBMDO</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0163-1829</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Physical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors present an efficient scheme for calcg. the Kohn-Sham ground state of metallic systems using pseudopotentials and a plane-wave basis set.  In the first part the application of Pulay's DIIS method (direct inversion in the iterative subspace) to the iterative diagonalization of large matrixes will be discussed.  This approach is stable, reliable, and minimizes the no. of order Natoms3 operations.  In the second part, we will discuss an efficient mixing scheme also based on Pulay's scheme.  A special "metric" and a special "preconditioning" optimized for a plane-wave basis set will be introduced.  Scaling of the method will be discussed in detail for non-self-consistent and self-consistent calcns.  It will be shown that the no. of iterations required to obtain a specific precision is almost independent of the system size.  Altogether an order Natoms2 scaling is found for systems contg. up to 1000 electrons.  If we take into account that the no. of k points can be decreased linearly with the system size, the overall scaling can approach Natoms.  They have implemented these algorithms within a powerful package called VASP (Vienna ab initio simulation package).  The program and the techniques have been used successfully for a large no. of different systems (liq. and amorphous semiconductors, liq. simple and transition metals, metallic and semiconducting surfaces, phonons in simple metals, transition metals, and semiconductors) and turned out to be very reliable.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoK9e6g4dZiorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg2z__9-3TzQA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK28Xms1Whu7Y%253D&amp;md5=9c8f6f298fe5ffe37c2589d3f970a697</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevLett.77.3865"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Perdew, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A physics-based side-reaction coupled electrochem. model for capacity fade of a graphite/LiMn2O4 cell is developed by including the key degrdn. mechanisms in both anode and cathode.  The side reactions considered in this study include (a) solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) growth and manganese deposition on the anode and (b) manganese dissoln., electrolyte oxidn. and salt decompn. on the cathode.  Our study reveals three stages of capacity fade upon long-term cycling: acceleration, stabilization, and satn.  In the acceleration stage, capacity fade is due mainly to the cyclable lithium loss induced by the anode SEI growth.  In the stabilization stage, the anode SEI growth slows down as it gets thicker, the cathode Mn dissoln.-induced capacity loss outpaces cyclable lithium loss, and the cathode becomes more intercalated at the end of discharge.  In the satn. stage, cathode capacity degrades further and becomes the limiting factor, the cyclable lithium is shifted to the anode and the cathode reaches end-of-discharge satn. due to the severe cathode capacity fade.  This study shows that the cyclable lithium loss and the cathode capacity loss are the two major contributors to the cell capacity fade, and the interaction between them dets. the cell capacity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpBV2iuMiI7ubVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj123tvJO7YlA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhslCjsbbO&amp;md5=1f6614595525617cd05618f5e1091dd0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1063/1.1323224"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Henkelman, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jónsson, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Improved tangent estimate in the nudged elastic band method for finding minimum energy paths and saddle points</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">An improved way of estg. the local tangent in the nudged elastic band method for finding min. energy paths is presented.  In systems where the force along the min. energy path is large compared to the restoring force perpendicular to the path and when many images of the system are included in the elastic band, kinks can develop and prevent the band from converging to the min. energy path.  We show how the kinks arise and present an improved way of estg. the local tangent which solves the problem.  The task of finding an accurate energy and configuration for the saddle point is also discussed and examples given where a complementary method, the dimer method, is used to efficiently converge to the saddle point.  Both methods only require the first deriv. of the energy and can, therefore, easily be applied in plane wave based d.-functional theory calcns.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Dual 2D CuSe/g-C3N4 heterostructure for boosting electrocatalytic reduction of CO2</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Hao; Ouyang, Tianwei; Li, Jiamin; Mu, Manman; Yin, Xiaohong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">CO2 Redn. Reaction (CO2RR) is an effective route to convert CO2 to value-added products in energy and environment.  CuSe/g-C3N4 electrodes were synthesized by anchoring hexagonal CuSe nanoplates on g-C3N4 nanosheets and used for electrochem. CO2RR.  Among the as-prepd. electrodes, 50% CuSe on g-C3N4 performed the highest faradaic efficiency of 85.28% to achieve 1.47 times higher than that of the pure CuSe NPs at -1.2 V vs.: RHE due to the larger specific area provided by the introduction of planar-structure g-C3N4 NSs and faster electron transfer speed on the interface of CuSe NPs and g-C3N4 NSs.  Meanwhile the calcns. of d. functional theory confirmed the electronic coupling on the electrodes to form an internal elec. field between two materials and electron direction from g-C3N4 NSs to CuSe NPs.  This work created a novel opportunity for optimizing design of electrode materials to enhance the CO selectivity of CO2RR.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoqc-VDrHcTqbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj123tvJO7YlA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhsVGrurnP&amp;md5=3b7b4259e8e25518a409de570f80ceb4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2017.04.082"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Iqbal, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bahadur, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Saeed, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shoaib, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Waqas, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrochemical performance of 2D polyaniline anchored CuS/Graphene nano-active composite as anode material for lithium-ion battery</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Li-ion battery (LIB) is a revolutionary step in the elec. energy storage technol. for making green environment.  A LIB anode material was constructed by using graphene/polyaniline/CuS nanocomposite (GR/PANI/CuS NC) as a high-performance electrode.  Initially, pure covellite CuS nanoplates (NPs) of the hexagonal structure were synthesized by hydrothermal route and then GR/PANI/CuS NC was fabricated by in-situ polymn. of aniline in the presence of CuS NPs and graphene nanosheets (GR NSs) as host matrix.  GR/PANI/CuS NC-based LIB showed the superior reversible current capacity of 1255 mA-h g-1, a high cycling stability with &gt;99% coulombic efficiency over 250 cycles even at a high c.d. of 5 Ag-1, low vol. expansion, and excellent power capabilities.  Galvanostatic charge/discharge tests and cyclic voltammetry anal. were used to study electrochem. properties.  The electrochem. test proves that GR/PANI/CuS NC is promising anode material for LIB.  The crystal phases and purity of the GR/PANI/CuS NC were confirmed by XRD.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultra thin CuSe nanosheets as the anode for sodium ion battery with high rate performance and long cycle life</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Dengfeng; Wei, Xinsong; Zhao, Di; Gao, Shuwen; Zhao, Gongyuan; Zhang, Hong; Li, Zhuo; Yu, Miao; Sun, Ye</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have quickly developed to be important alternative energy storage devices other than lithium-ion batteries in the explosively growing market of large-scale grid storage and low-speed elec. vehicles, thanks to their low cost and the abundance of sodium resources.  However, the sluggish sodiation kinetics remains major concerns in design of competent anode materials for SIBs.  Herein, by using a one-step, facile hydrothermal synthesis, well-defined ultra thin CuSe nanosheets (thickness of ∼5 nm) were fabricated, leading to a narrow band gap, flexible Cu-Se bonding and abundant electrochem. active sites.  As a result, the product presents high rate performance: a high capacity of 404 mAh g-1 is achieved at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1 after 100 operation cycles, and the capacity can be maintained to 276 mAh g-1 even at a high c.d. of 20 A g-1.  According to kinetics anal., surface capacitance contributes dominatly in the electrochem. process, facilitating fast sodiation.  Moreover, coordinated the ultra thin thickness and two-dimensional morphol. of the nanosheets with their three-dimensional open framework, the vol. expansion-related issues during charge/discharge processes have been well addressed, resulting in ultrahigh cycling stability (with 100% capacity maintenance after 500 cycles at 0.5 A g-1) together with ultra long cycle life (up to 10,000 working cycles) at 20 A g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoFpZzwAVYeGbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgX04zMKbSYBw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly infiltrative micro-sized Cu2Se as advanced material with excellent rate performance and ultralong cycle-life for sodium ion half/full batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shao, Lianyi; Wang, Shige; Qi, Jianpeng; Sun, Zhipeng; Shi, Xiaoyan; Shi, Yuansheng; Lu, Xia</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today Physics</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Appropriate material is the key to improve the energy and power d. of sodium ion batteries.  Herein, monoclinic Cu2Se is acquired by a facile one-pot solid method using Cu foil and Se power as the raw materials without use of expensive reagents and sophisticated instruments.  Cu2Se exhibits preeminent cycling and rate properties.  Concretely, Cu2Se represents reversible capacity of 264 and 241 mAh g-1 at 0.1 and 10 A g-1, as well as high capacity retention of ≈100% over 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1.  When Cu2Se is applied as anode to assemble full battery with Na3V2(PO4)2F3@rGO, this battery exhibits a largest energy d. of 97 Wh kg-1 (with a power d. of 117 W kg-1) and a biggest power d. of 1180 W kg-1 (with energy d. of 59 Wh kg-1) based on the gross mass of cathode and anode active materials.  A combination of ex-situ X-ray diffraction, transition electron microscopy tests and first-principle calcns. demonstrate a reversible transformation between Cu2Se and Cu exists in the discharge-charge process.  Stable solid-electrolyte interface film, highly infiltrative electrode and capacitive Na + storage behaviors are in favor of the excellent property.  The preeminent electrochem. performance indicates that Cu2Se is a highly desirable anode material for high-performance sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr_i4CP0OZM2bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgX04zMKbSYBw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhtF2lsrjO&amp;md5=2a510a48edb8b87e15714ef79dd6e7cd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.0c03432"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ran, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gentle, I.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Biomimetic Sn4P3 Anchored on Carbon Nanotubes as an Anode for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ran, Lingbing; Luo, Bin; Gentle, Ian R.; Lin, Tongen; Sun, Qiang; Li, Ming; Rana, Md Masud; Wang, Lianzhou; Knibbe, Ruth</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, Sn4P3 has emerged as a promising anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to the high specific capacity.  However, the use of Sn4P3 has been impeded by capacity fade and an inferior rate performance.  Herein, a biomimetic heterostructure is reported by using a simple hydrothermal reaction followed by thermal treatment.  This bottlebrush-like structure consists of a stem-like carbon nanotube (CNT) as the electron expressway and mech. support; fructus-like Sn4P3 nanoparticles as the active material; and the permeable stoma-like thin carbon coating as the buffer layer.  Having benefited from the biomimetic structure, a superior electrochem. performance is obtained in the SIBs.  It exhibits a high capacity of 742 mA h g-1 after 150 cycles at 0.2C, and superior rate performance with 449 mA h g-1 at 2C after 500 cycles.  Moreover, the sodium storage mechanism is confirmed by cyclic voltammetry and ex situ X-ray diffraction and transmission electron microscopy.  In situ electrochem. impedance spectroscopy was adopted to analyze the reaction dynamics.  This research represents a further step toward figuring out the inferior electrochem. performance of other metal phosphide materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqi0vlL0Pw9D7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgX04zMKbSYBw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsVSiu7bP&amp;md5=521acacd64cd8786ae3120281a0139d9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ju, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sb<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>@Sb nanoparticles impregnated in N-doped carbon microcages for ultralong life and high-rate sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>9</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">12169</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">12178</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/D1TA01930A</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D9%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D12169-12178%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DA.%2BXu%26author%3DC.%2BHuang%26author%3DG.%2BLi%26author%3DK.%2BZou%26author%3DH.%2BSun%26author%3DL.%2BFu%26author%3DJ.%2BJu%26author%3DY.%2BSong%26author%3DS.%2BWu%26author%3DZ.%2BXu%26author%3DY.%2BYan%26title%3DSb2O3%2540Sb%2Bnanoparticles%2Bimpregnated%2Bin%2BN-doped%2Bcarbon%2Bmicrocages%2Bfor%2Bultralong%2Blife%2Band%2Bhigh-rate%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FD1TA01930A&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.2c20655&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FD1TA01930A&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sb2O3@Sb nanoparticles impregnated in N-doped carbon microcages for ultralong life and high-rate sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Anding; Huang, Chuyun; Li, Guilan; Zou, Kaixiang; Sun, Hao; Fu, Lili; Ju, Jiahao; Song, Yang; Wu, Songping; Xu, Zhiguang; Yan, Yurong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12169-12178</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony-based materials have been considered as highly competitive anodes for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) because of their high theor. capacity.  However, the poor rate capability and fast capacity fading, originating from sluggish kinetics and vol. expansion, greatly restrict their practical application.  To address the above issues, an effective spraying method and one-step partial redn. process were utilized to synthesize Sb2O3@Sb nanoparticle impregnated in N-doped carbon microcages (Sb2O3@Sb@NC) offering extraordinary sodium storage capabilities and delivering an ultra-high rate performance of 175.1 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1 and a superior capacity retention of 245.2 mA h g-1 after 10 000 cycles under 10 A g-1 for SIBs.  Such unprecedented electrochem. properties of the Sb2O3@Sb@NC electrode can be ascribed to the comprehensive characteristics derived from multi-scale structural engineering: the fast electrochem. kinetics and tight packing of Sb2O3@Sb nanoparticles with carbon sheets, the strong Na+ adsorption ability of Sb2O3@Sb@NC enhanced by the synergistic effect of heterostructures and N-doping, the structural integrity strengthened by a robust interface bond of Sb-O-C, and the improved pseudocapacitive contribution.  These distinct features enable the Sb2O3@Sb@NC anode to be a potential candidate for large-scale sodium ion storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRxKNkTwl2DrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhkw20UH1kT_w"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXptFyrsbY%253D&amp;md5=18d0eb0a20f15c0ea2855d6ebe55c905</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da89cd5ed6b325-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44'],'ref45':['cit45'],'ref46':['cit46']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrahigh rate performance of hollow antimony nanoparticles impregnated in open carbon boxes for sodium-ion battery under elevated temperature</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Anding; Xia, Qi; Zhang, Shenkui; Duan, Huanhuan; Yan, Yurong; Wu, Songping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony is a competitive and promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) due to its high theor. capacity.  However, the poor rate capability and fast capacity fading greatly restrict its practical application.  To address the above issues, a facile and eco-friendly sacrificial template method is developed to synthesize hollow Sb nanoparticles impregnated in open carbon boxes (Sb HPs@OCB).  The as-obtained Sb HPs@OCB composite exhibits excellent sodium storage properties even when operated at an elevated temp. of 50°C, delivering a robust rate capability of 345 mAh g-1 at 16 A g-1 and rendering an outstanding reversible capacity of 187 mAh g-1 at a high rate of 10 A g-1 after 300 cycles.  Such superior electrochem. performance of the Sb HPs@OCB can be attributed to the comprehensive characteristics of improved kinetics derived from hollow Sb nanoparticles impregnated into 2D carbon nanowalls, the existence of robust Sb-O-C bond, and enhanced pseudocapacitive behavior.  All those factors enable Sb HPs@OCB great potential and distinct merit for large-scale energy storage of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr2x_05ZO4F9LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhalzUAYJmQbQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvVWktrfF&amp;md5=cea3cb2430f4e0dfe9dc1e559d690941</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201809195"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Multicore–Shell Bi@N-doped Carbon Nanospheres for High Power Density and Long Cycle Life Sodium- and Potassium-Ion Anodes</span>. <i>Adv.                         rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Extremely stable antimony-carbon composite anodes for potassium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zheng, Jing; Yang, Yong; Fan, Xiulin; Ji, Guangbin; Ji, Xiao; Wang, Haiyang; Hou, Singyuk; Zachariah, Michael R.; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Potassium-ion batteries (PIBs) have been considered as promising alternatives to lithium-ion batteries due to potassium's high natural abundance of 2.09 wt% (vs. 0.0017 wt% for Li) and K/K+ having a low redox potential of -2.93 V (vs. -2.71 V for Na/Na+).  However, PIB electrodes still suffer huge challenges due to the large K-ion radius and slow reaction dynamics.  Herein, we report a high-capacity Sb@CSN composite anode with Sb nanoparticles uniformly encapsulated by a carbon sphere network (CSN) for PIBs.  First-principles computations and electrochem. characterization confirm a reversible sequential phase transformation of KSb2, KSb, K5Sb4, and K3Sb during the potassiation/depotassiation process.  In a concd. 4 M KTFSI/EC + DEC electrolyte, the Sb@CSN anode delivers a high reversible capacity of 551 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles with an extremely slow capacity decay of only 0.06% per cycle from the 10th to 100th cycle; when at a high c.d. of 200 mA g-1, the Sb@CSN anode still maintains a capacity of 504 mA h g-1 after 220 cycles.  The Sb@CSN anodes demonstrate one of the best electrochem. performances for all K-ion battery anodes reported to date.  The exceptional performance of Sb@CSN should be attributed to the efficient encapsulation of small Sb nanoparticles in the conductive carbon network as well as the formation of a robust KF-rich SEI layer on the Sb@CSN anode in the concd. 4 M KTFSI/EC + DEC electrolyte.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoYTdp9SpJZJ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhalzUAYJmQbQ"> &gt;&gt;                         rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Optimizing the Void Size of Yolk-Shell Bi@Void@C Nanospheres for High-Power-Density Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Hai; Chen, Lin-Wei; He, Fuxiang; Zhang, Jiaqing; Feng, Yuezhan; Zhao, Lukang; Wang, Bin; He, Lixin; Zhang, Qiaobao; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">20</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">758-767</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Bi was demonstrated as a promising anode for Na-ion batteries (NIBs) because it has high gravimetry (386 mA-h g-1) and volumetric capacity (3800 mA-h cm-3).  However, Bi suffers from large vol. expansion during sodiation, leading to poor electrochem. performance.  The construction of a nanostructure with sufficient void space to accommodate the vol. change was proven effective for achieving prolonged cycling stability.  However the excessive void space will definitely decrease the volumetric energy d. of the battery.  Herein, the authors design optimized Bi@Void@C nanospheres (Bi@Void@C-2) with yolk-shell structure that exhibit the best cycling performance and enhanced volumetric energy d.  The optimized void space not only could buffer the vol. change of the Bi nanosphere but also could keep the high volumetric energy d. of the battery.  The Bi@Void@C-2 shows an excellent rate capacity of 173 mA-h g-1 at ultrahigh c.d. of 100 A g-1 and long-cycle life (198 mA-h g-1 at 20 A g-1 over 10,000 cycles).  The origin of the superior performance is achieved through in-depth fundamental studies during battery operation using in situ XRD and in situ transmission electron microscope (TEM), complemented by theor. calcns. and ex situ TEM observation.  The rational design provides insights for anode materials with large vol. variation, esp. for conversion type and alloying type mechanism materials for batteries (i.e., Li-ion batteries, Na-ion batteries).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqYnOlKB-gRV7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljryNNjBAxpBw"> &gt;&gt; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, C.</span></span>;             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb materials have considered to be one of the most excellent anode materials for sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  Developing a Sb-based materials with high-rate long-term cycling durability is highly requisite for boosting their practical application as SIB anodes.  In this work, yolk-shell structured Sb@C nanoconfined nitrogen-sulfur co-doped 3D porous carbon microspheres (Sb@NS-3DPCMSs) were prepd. via salt-templating directed spray-drying strategy combined with ingenious and continuous high efficiency one-pot multi-step approach.  The formation mechanism of the yolk-shell structure was revealed by first-principles simulations for the first time.  In the constructed 3D architecture, the robust yolk-shell structure for confining Sb nanocrystals can provide enough void space for effectively buffering the vol. expansion of Sb and thus remarkably stabilize the structural integrity of the overall electrode during rapid long-term cycling, while the interconnected empty carbon box with abundant hierarchical pores and high cond. can facilitate the fast transport of electrons, sodium ions and electrolyte in the whole electrode.  Moreover, nitrogen-sulfur co-doping can enhance the intercalation kinetics of sodium ions, and further increase the capacity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrvBVXjL2awf7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljryNNjBAxpBw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvFSqt7bM&amp;md5=490570aed05dffe02faf06facd39d792</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202001976"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kong, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.-H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Rational Design of Sb@C@TiO<sub>2</sub> Triple-Shell Nanoboxes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2001976</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rational Design of Sb@C@TiO2 Triple-Shell Nanoboxes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kong, Ming; Liu, Yan; Zhou, Bin; Yang, Kaixuan; Tang, Jianfeng; Zhang, Ping; Zhang, Wen-Hua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony is an attractive anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to its high theor. capacity and appropriate sodiation potential.  However, its practical application is severely impeded by its poor cycling stability caused by dramatic volumetric variations during sodium uptake and release processes.  Here, to circumvent this obstacle, Sb@C@TiO2 triple-shell nanoboxes (TSNBs) are synthesized through a template-engaged galvanic replacement approach.  The TSNB structure consists of an inner Sb hollow nanobox protected by a conductive carbon middle shell and a TiO2-nanosheet-constructed outer shell.  This structure offers dual protection to the inner Sb and enough room to accommodate vol. expansion, thus promoting the structural integrity of the electrode and the formation of a stable solid-electrolyte interface film.  Benefiting from the rational structural design and synergistic effects of Sb, carbon, and TiO2, the Sb@C@TiO2 electrode exhibits superior rate performance (212 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1) and outstanding long-term cycling stability (193 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 after 4000 cycles).  Moreover, a full cell assembled with a configuration of Sb@C@TiO2//Na3(VOPO4)2F displays a high output voltage of 2.8 V and a high energy d. of 179 Wh kg-1, revealing the great promise of Sb@C@TiO2 TSNBs as the electrode in SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGreTfLplDLzwrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljryNNjBAxpBw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvFWmtbjJ&amp;md5=de9e2211b9e6d06ee5f518432acb5661</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c17040"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Confining MoSe<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets into N-Doped Hollow Porous Carbon Microspheres for Fast-Charged and Long-Life Potassium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The potassium-ion battery (PIB) is the most promising alternative to a lithium-ion battery (LIB).  Exploitation of a suitable electrode material is crucial to promote the development of PIBs.  The MoSe2 material has attracted much attention due to its high theor. capacity, unique layered structure, and good cond.  However, the potassium storage property of MoSe2 has been suffering from structural fragmentation and sluggish reaction kinetic caused by large potassium ions upon insertion/extn., which needs to be further improved. The excellent electrochem. performance can be attributed to unique structure, N-doping, and robust chem. bonds.  The storage mechanism of MoSe2 for potassium ions was explored.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Urchin-like CoSe2 assembled by nanorods was synthesized via simple solvothermal route and was 1st applied as an anode material for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) with ether-based electrolytes.  The CoSe2 delivers excellent sodiation and de-sodiation properties when using 1 M NaCF3SO3 in diethyleneglycol dimethylether as an electrolyte and cycling between 0.5 and 3.0 V.  A high discharge capacity of 0.410 A h g-1 is obtained at 1 A g-1 after 1800 cycles, corresponding to a capacity retention of 98.6% calcd. from the 30th cycle. During the charge process, Co 1st reacts with Na2Se to form NaxCoSe2 and then turns back to CoSe2.  In addn. to Na/CoSe2 half cells, Na3V2(PO4)3/CoSe2 full cell with excessive amt. of Na3V2(PO4)3 was studied.  The full cell exhibits a reversible capacity of 0.380 Ah g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as a promising candidate to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) owing to the inexpensive and abundant sodium reserves.  However, the application of anode materials for SIBs still confront rapid capacity fading and undesirable rate capability.  Here we simultaneously grow ultrafine ZnSe nanoparticles on the inner walls and the outer surface of hollow carbon nanospheres (ZnSe@HCNs), giving a unique hierarchical hybrid nanostructure that can sustain a capacity of 361.9 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1 over 1000 cycles and 266.5 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1.  Our investigations indicate that the sodium storage mechanism of ZnSe@HCNs electrodes is a mixt. of alloying and conversion reactions, where ZnSe converts to Na2Se and NaZn13 through a series of intermediate compds.  Also, a full cell is constructed from our designed ZnSe@HCNs anode and Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode.  It delivers a reversible discharge capacity of about 313.1 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.5 A g-1 with high Columbic efficiency over 98.2%.  The outstanding sodium storage of as-prepd. ZnSe@HCNs is attributed to the confinement of ZnSe structural changes both inside/outside of hollow nanospheres during the sodiation/desodiation processes.  Our work offers a promising design to enable high-power-d. electrodes for the various battery systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2lXm2W3SJvLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljryNNjBAxpBw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXlt1yqtL0%253D&amp;md5=39895f776821cb0a0b91b85a640c079f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2019.05.039"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In-situ rooting ZnSe/N-doped hollow carbon architectures as high-rate and long-life anode materials for half/full sodium-ion and potassium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>23</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">35</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">45</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        rightTab-cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Achieving Ultrafast and Stable Na-Ion Storage in FeSe2 Nanorods/Graphene Anodes by Controlling the Surface Oxide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Dan; Zhou, Jisheng; Chen, Xiaohong; Song, Huaihe</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">26</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">22841-22850</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Designing transitional metal selenides (TMSes) with superior rate and cyclic performance for sodium-ion storage remains great challenges.  To achieve this task, the influence of surface oxides on Na-ion storage behavior of FeSe2 is investigated by designing FeSe2 with varying oxide content.  It is found that surface oxide has an inhibitory effect on the activity of FeSe2.  Small-sized FeSe2 on graphene with higher surface oxide content exhibits obviously inferior performance compared to large-sized FeSe2 with lower oxide content.  By controlling oxide content, the prepd. FeSe2 nanorods/graphene exhibits a high capacity of 459 mAh/g at 0.1 A/g and superior rate performance.  Only 10% capacity decrease occurs with the increase in c.d. from 0.1 to 5 A/g.  Even at 25 A/g (∼50 C), it delivers a capacity of 227 mAh/g with almost no decay after 800 cycles.  The influence mechanism of surface oxide is investigated.  The oxide can be converted to a sodiated shell with high mech. strength and poor cond., which generates phase-transition resistance to suppress the sodiation of FeSe2 core, blocks the transfer of Na-ions and electrons in subsequent sodiation processes.  Understanding the effect of surface oxide on Na-ion storage will be helpful in designing TMSes and other active materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqaBlVnT1ymz7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljVtfrq6t62UA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhtFSrsbnI&amp;md5=913bebda42e3d31c2a5910bf797009be</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1002/advs.202104630"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.-P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, F.-Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In Situ Fabrication of Cuprous Selenide Electrode via Selenization of Copper Current Collector for High-Efficiency Potassium-Ion and Sodium-Ion Storage</span>. <i>Adv.
